<li>In the 1994-1995 <a href="/wiki/Television_syndication" class="mw-redirect" title="Television syndication">syndicated television</a> block <i><a href="/wiki/The_Marvel_Action_Hour" title="The Marvel Action Hour">The Marvel Action Hour</a></i>, Lee appeared as himself to give brief introductions to each episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_(TV_series)" title="Iron Man (TV series)">Iron Man</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Fantastic_Four_(1994_TV_series)" title="Fantastic Four (1994 TV series)">Fantastic Four</a></i> animated series.</li>
<li>Lee has an extensive cameo in the 1995 <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Smith" title="Kevin Smith">Kevin Smith</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Mallrats" title="Mallrats">Mallrats</a></i>. He plays himself, this time visiting the mall to sign books at a comic store. Later, he takes on the role of a sage-like character, giving <a href="/wiki/Jason_Lee_(actor)" title="Jason Lee (actor)">Jason Lee</a>'s character, Brodie Bruce (a longtime fan of Stan's), advice on his love life. He also recorded interviews with Smith for the non-fiction video <i><a href="/wiki/Stan_Lee%27s_Mutants,_Monsters_%26_Marvels" title="Stan Lee's Mutants, Monsters &amp; Marvels">Stan Lee's Mutants, Monsters &amp; Marvels</a></i> (2002). Lee will make a second cameo in Smith's 2016 film <i><a href="/wiki/Yoga_Hosers" title="Yoga Hosers">Yoga Hosers</a></i> as a police officer.</li>
<li>Lee is the host of the 2010 <a href="/wiki/History_(U.S._TV_channel)" title="History (U.S. TV channel)">History Channel</a> documentary series <i><a href="/wiki/Stan_Lee%27s_Superhumans" title="Stan Lee's Superhumans">Stan Lee's Superhumans</a></i>.</li>
<li>Lee plays himself in the 2011 Frankie Muniz film <i><a href="/wiki/Pizza_Man_(2011_film)" title="Pizza Man (2011 film)">Pizza Man</a></i>.</li>
<li>Lee makes a cameo appearance as the "Three Stooges Wedding Guest" in the 2004 <a href="/wiki/Disney" class="mw-redirect" title="Disney">Disney</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Princess_Diaries_2:_Royal_Engagement" title="The Princess Diaries 2: Royal Engagement">The Princess Diaries 2: Royal Engagement</a></i>.</li>
<li>Lee hosted and judged contestants in the <a href="/wiki/SyFy" class="mw-redirect" title="SyFy">SyFy</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Be_a_Superhero%3F" title="Who Wants to Be a Superhero?">Who Wants to Be a Superhero?</a></i></li>
<li>Lee appears with director Kevin Smith and 2000s Marvel editor-in-chief <a href="/wiki/Joe_Quesada" title="Joe Quesada">Joe Quesada</a> in the DVD program <i>Marvel Then &amp; Now: An Evening with Stan Lee and Joe Quesada, hosted by Kevin Smith</i>.</li>
<li>Lee was interviewed on the <a href="/wiki/History_Channel" class="mw-redirect" title="History Channel">History Channel</a> show <i>Superhuman</i> by Daniel Browning Smith, who held several Guinness Records for extreme flexibility<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> due to having <a href="/wiki/Ehlers-Danlos_syndrome" class="mw-redirect" title="Ehlers-Danlos syndrome">Ehlers-Danlos syndrome</a>, a genetic condition affecting collagen formation. Smith had created his own comic book to display his own struggles as an outcast for his flexibility, and legitimately surprised Lee with a quick demonstration of his talent.</li>
<li>In the animated series <i><a href="/wiki/Jim_Henson%27s_Muppet_Babies" class="mw-redirect" title="Jim Henson's Muppet Babies">Jim Henson's Muppet Babies</a></i>, Lee plays himself in a live-action scene of the "<a href="/wiki/List_of_Muppet_Babies_episodes#Season_6_.281989.29" title="List of Muppet Babies episodes">Comic Capers</a>" episode.</li>
<li>Lee appeared as himself in an extended self-parodying sketch on the episode "<a href="/wiki/Tapping_a_Hero" class="mw-redirect" title="Tapping a Hero">Tapping a Hero</a>" of <i><a href="/wiki/Robot_Chicken" title="Robot Chicken">Robot Chicken</a></i>.</li>
<li>Lee appears as himself in writer-director <a href="/wiki/Larry_Cohen" title="Larry Cohen">Larry Cohen</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ambulance" title="The Ambulance">The Ambulance</a></i> (1990), in which <a href="/wiki/Eric_Roberts" title="Eric Roberts">Eric Roberts</a> plays an aspiring comics artist.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup></li>
<li>In "<a href="/wiki/I_Am_Furious_(Yellow)" title="I Am Furious (Yellow)">I Am Furious (Yellow)</a>", a <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_13)" title="The Simpsons (season 13)">season 13</a> episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i>, Lee voices an animated version of himself, who is a prolonged visitor to <a href="/wiki/Comic_Book_Guy" title="Comic Book Guy">Comic Book Guy</a>'s store. He asks if Comic Book Guy is the stalker of <a href="/wiki/Lynda_Carter" title="Lynda Carter">Lynda Carter</a> – the star of the 1970s show <i><a href="/wiki/Wonder_Woman_(TV_series)" title="Wonder Woman (TV series)">Wonder Woman</a></i> – and shows signs of <a href="/wiki/Dementia" title="Dementia">dementia</a>, such as breaking a customer's toy <a href="/wiki/Batmobile" title="Batmobile">Batmobile</a> by trying to cram a <a href="/wiki/Thing_(comics)" title="Thing (comics)">Thing</a> <a href="/wiki/Action_figure" title="Action figure">action figure</a> into it (claiming that he "made it better"), hiding <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">DC</a> comics behind Marvel comics, and believing that he is the Hulk (and fails trying to become the Hulk, while Comic Book Guy comments he couldn't even change into <a href="/wiki/Bill_Bixby" title="Bill Bixby">Bill Bixby</a>). Lee also appeared on the <a href="/wiki/Audio_commentary" title="Audio commentary">commentary track</a> along with other <i>Simpsons</i> writers and directors on the episode for <i>The Simpsons</i> Season 13 box set released in 2010. In a later episode, "<a href="/wiki/Worst_Episode_Ever" title="Worst Episode Ever">Worst Episode Ever</a>", Lee's picture is seen next to several others on the wall behind the register, under the heading "Banned for life". Lee later officiated Comic Book Guy's wedding to a lovely <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">manga</a> artist in "<a href="/wiki/Married_to_the_Blob" title="Married to the Blob">Married to the Blob</a>".</li>
<li>Lee appears as himself in <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hamill" title="Mark Hamill">Mark Hamill</a>'s 2004 film <i><a href="/wiki/Comic_Book:_The_Movie" title="Comic Book: The Movie">Comic Book: The Movie</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Direct-to-video" title="Direct-to-video">direct-to-video</a> mockumentary primarily filmed at the 2002 <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con" title="San Diego Comic-Con">San Diego Comic-Con</a>.</li>
<li>Lee made an appearance on December 21, 2006, on the <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> game show <i><a href="/wiki/Identity_(game_show)" title="Identity (game show)">Identity</a></i>.</li>
<li>Lee appeared as himself in "The Excelsior Acquisition", a <a href="/wiki/The_Big_Bang_Theory_(season_3)" title="The Big Bang Theory (season 3)">third season</a> episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Big_Bang_Theory" title="The Big Bang Theory">The Big Bang Theory</a></i>, in March 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> He appears at the front door of his house wearing Fantastic Four pajamas, ultimately calling back into the house, "Joanie, call the police!" to get rid of <a href="/wiki/Sheldon_Cooper" title="Sheldon Cooper">Sheldon</a>, who showed up after missing a comic book signing at the local store and ordered a <a href="/wiki/Restraining_order" title="Restraining order">restraining order</a> against him.</li>
<li>He plays a bus driver in the sixteenth episode of the first season of <i><a href="/wiki/Heroes_(TV_series)" title="Heroes (TV series)">Heroes</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee made a guest appearance as himself in "Bottom's Up", a <a href="/wiki/List_of_celebrities_appearing_on_Entourage#Season_7_.282010.29" title="List of celebrities appearing on Entourage">season seven episode</a> of the TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Entourage_(U.S._TV_series)" title="Entourage (U.S. TV series)">Entourage</a></i>.</li>
<li>He guest-starred as Dr. Lee (aka: Generalissimo) in "Glimpse", a season four episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Eureka_(U.S._TV_series)" title="Eureka (U.S. TV series)">Eureka</a></i> that aired in July 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee appears in "<a href="/wiki/Nikita_(season_1)#ep5" title="Nikita (season 1)">The Guardian</a>", the October 7, 2010, episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Nikita_(2010_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Nikita (2010 TV series)">Nikita</a></i>, as Hank Excelsior, a witness to a bank robbery who is interviewed by a TV reporter.</li>
<li>Lee was interviewed in the 2011 documentary <i>Superheroes</i>.</li>
<li>Lee appears in <a href="/wiki/X_Japan" title="X Japan">X Japan</a>'s unreleased music video for their song "<a href="/wiki/Born_to_Be_Free_(X_Japan_song)" title="Born to Be Free (X Japan song)">Born to Be Free</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee portrayed himself at a CIA holiday party in the <a href="/wiki/Chuck_(season_5)" title="Chuck (season 5)">fifth season</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Chuck_(TV_series)" title="Chuck (TV series)">Chuck</a></i>, in which it is revealed in that universe he secretly works for the government and has a romantic interest in <a href="/wiki/Diane_Beckman" title="Diane Beckman">General Beckman</a>.</li>
<li>Lee appeared in the eleventh episode of season five of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guild_(web_series)" title="The Guild (web series)">The Guild</a></i>, in which he was captured at a convention by the character Zaboo's <a href="/wiki/Master_Chief_(Halo)" title="Master Chief (Halo)">Master Chief</a> cosplaying henchmen.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee lent his voice to "The Amazing Man-Spider", a segment of the May 13, 2013 episode of the satirical animated TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Mad_(TV_series)" title="Mad (TV series)">MAD</a></i>. The segment depicts the story of what happened to the radioactive spider that bit Peter Parker.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee portrayed a future version of Tony Stark in "Episode 205 – The Future!" of the comedy web series <i>Avengers Assemble!</i>. In this episode, he delivered from the future a cryptic message to the rest of his fellow Avengers, but constantly frustrated his companions due to his ineptness with the technology of his future era.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup></li>
<li>He was the subject of an April 2012 <a href="/wiki/Epix_(TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Epix (TV channel)">Epix</a> cable-network documentary, "With Great Power: The Stan Lee Story.”<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee appeared as a judge in the second season premiere of the web series <i><a href="/wiki/Video_Game_High_School" title="Video Game High School">Video Game High School</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup></li>
<li>In the <i><a href="/wiki/Phineas_and_Ferb" title="Phineas and Ferb">Phineas and Ferb</a></i> crossover special, <i><a href="/wiki/Phineas_and_Ferb:_Mission_Marvel" title="Phineas and Ferb: Mission Marvel">Mission Marvel</a></i>, Lee cameos as a New York City hot dog vendor.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee is among the interview subjects in <i>Superheroes: A Never-Ending Battle</i>, a three-hour documentary narrated by <a href="/wiki/Liev_Schreiber" title="Liev Schreiber">Liev Schreiber</a>, which premiered on <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a> in October 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee's <i><a href="/wiki/Chakra_the_Invincible" class="mw-redirect" title="Chakra the Invincible">Chakra the Invincible</a></i> was scheduled to premiere on <a href="/wiki/Rovio_Entertainment" title="Rovio Entertainment">Rovio Entertainment</a>'s ToonsTV channel in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-hollywoodreporter1_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hollywoodreporter1-176">[175]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee filmed a cameo in the 2010 film <i><a href="/wiki/Kick-Ass_(film)" title="Kick-Ass (film)">Kick-Ass</a></i>, as a man watching news footage of the title character but was cut out from the film.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee made a brief cameo in the 2014 animated film <i><a href="/wiki/Jay_%26_Silent_Bob%27s_Super_Groovy_Cartoon_Movie" title="Jay &amp; Silent Bob's Super Groovy Cartoon Movie">Jay &amp; Silent Bob's Super Groovy Cartoon Movie</a></i>. During his appearance, Lee visits <a href="/wiki/Bluntman_and_Chronic" title="Bluntman and Chronic">Bluntman and Chronic</a> to talk to them about the "<a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">Avenger Initiative</a>".</li>
<li>Lee made a cameo in Bart Baker's parody of "<a href="/wiki/Elastic_Heart" title="Elastic Heart">Elastic Heart</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Sia_(musician)" title="Sia (musician)">Sia</a> when he bails Sia (played by Amanda Hosler) out of jail for the pedophilia in her Elastic Heart video to star in her own superhero movie with <a href="/wiki/Shia_LaBeouf" title="Shia LaBeouf">Shia LaBeouf</a> (played by Baker) and <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> (played by Warren Barrow) as the main villain.</li>
<li>Lee appears several times in the refurbished version of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Adventures_of_Spider-Man" title="The Amazing Adventures of Spider-Man">The Amazing Adventures of Spider-Man</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee was slated to portray himself in the <a href="/wiki/Sequel" title="Sequel">sequel</a> to <i>Mallrats</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mallbrats" class="mw-redirect" title="Mallbrats">Mallbrats</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mewes-Lee-Rooker-confirmed_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mewes-Lee-Rooker-confirmed-179">[178]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee made a cameo appearance in a web-series called "Super Power Beat Down" where he plays a man reading a newspaper who tells Spider-Man and Darth Maul to keep the noise down or else he will get angry.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games_and_applications">Video games and applications</span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Lee narrates the 2000 video game <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_(2000_video_game)" title="Spider-Man (2000 video game)">Spider-Man</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup> the 2001 sequel <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_2:_Enter_Electro" title="Spider-Man 2: Enter Electro">Spider-Man 2: Enter Electro</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup> and 2010's <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man:_Shattered_Dimensions" title="Spider-Man: Shattered Dimensions">Spider-Man: Shattered Dimensions</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee made his first-ever onscreen video game appearance as a senator named after himself in <i><a href="/wiki/Marvel_Ultimate_Alliance_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Marvel Ultimate Alliance 2">Marvel Ultimate Alliance 2</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee narrates <i>The Avengers Origins: Hulk</i> and <i>Avengers Origins: Assemble!</i> apps for the <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">iPad</a>, <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a>, and <a href="/wiki/IPod_Touch" title="IPod Touch">iPod Touch</a>, which were released by <a href="/wiki/Disney_Publishing_Worldwide" title="Disney Publishing Worldwide">Disney Publishing Worldwide</a> in February 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee is a playable character in <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_(2012_video_game)" title="The Amazing Spider-Man (2012 video game)">The Amazing Spider-Man</a></i> video game, which was released in June 2012, as a tie-in to the <a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_(2012_film)" title="The Amazing Spider-Man (2012 film)">film of the same name</a>. In the game, Lee is depicted as having the same superpowers as Spider-Man, and uses them to retrieve the pages of a new comic book manuscript that he had lost and were subsequently scattered around Manhattan.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup> He also voices a character with his first name in the main story mode, who calls Peter about the charges to his credit card when Peter's walking to Dr. Connor's sewer lab.</li>
<li>Lee appears as a playable Lego version of himself in <i><a href="/wiki/Lego_Marvel_Super_Heroes" title="Lego Marvel Super Heroes">Lego Marvel Super Heroes</a></i> where he was able to turn into Stan-Hulk <sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup> released October 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lee reprised his role, appearing as himself in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_2_(2014_video_game)" title="The Amazing Spider-Man 2 (2014 video game)">The Amazing Spider-Man 2</a></i> video game, which was released in April 2014, as a tie-in to the <a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_2" title="The Amazing Spider-Man 2">film of the same name</a>.</li>
<li>Lee appears as a playable Lego version of himself in <i><a href="/wiki/Lego_Marvel%27s_Avengers" title="Lego Marvel's Avengers">Lego Marvel's Avengers</a></i> where he is able to turn into Stan-Hulk, Iron Stan and the StanBuster.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Lee was raised in a Jewish family. In a 2002 survey of whether he believes in God, he stated, "Well, let me put it this way... [Pauses.] No, I'm not going to try to be clever. I really don't know. I just don't know."<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>He married Joan Clayton Boocock on December 5, 1947,<sup id="cite_ref-autobio-p69_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autobio-p69-189">[188]</a></sup> and in 1949, the couple bought a two-story, three-bedroom home at 1084 West Broadway in <a href="/wiki/Woodmere,_New_York" title="Woodmere, New York">Woodmere, New York</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>, living there through 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup> Their daughter Joan Celia "J.C." Lee was born in 1950. Another child, Jan Lee, died three days after delivery in 1953.<sup id="cite_ref-LeeMair74_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeeMair74-191">[190]</a></sup> The Lees resided at 226 Richards Lane in the Long Island town of <a href="/wiki/Hewlett_Harbor,_New_York" title="Hewlett Harbor, New York">Hewlett Harbor, New York</a>, from 1952 to 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup> They also owned a two-bedroom <a href="/wiki/Condominium" title="Condominium">condominium</a> on the 14th floor of 220 East 63rd Street in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup> from 1975 to 1980 and a vacation home on Cutler Lane in <a href="/wiki/Remsenburg,_New_York" title="Remsenburg, New York">Remsenburg, New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup> For their move to the west coast in 1981, he and his wife bought a home in <a href="/wiki/West_Hollywood,_California" title="West Hollywood, California">West Hollywood, California</a> previously owned by comedian <a href="/wiki/Jack_Benny" title="Jack Benny">Jack Benny</a>'s radio announcer, <a href="/wiki/Don_Wilson_(announcer)" title="Don Wilson (announcer)">Don Wilson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>In late September 2012, Lee underwent a surgical operation to insert a <a href="/wiki/Pacemaker" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacemaker">pacemaker</a> into his body, cancelling planned appearances at conventions.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lee's favorite authors include <a href="/wiki/Stephen_King" title="Stephen King">Stephen King</a>, <a href="/wiki/H._G._Wells" title="H. G. Wells">H. G. Wells</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Twain" title="Mark Twain">Mark Twain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Conan_Doyle" title="Arthur Conan Doyle">Arthur Conan Doyle</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Charles Dickens</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Harlan_Ellison" title="Harlan Ellison">Harlan Ellison</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[197]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Lee's account of how he began working for Marvel's predecessor, Timely, has varied. He has said in lectures and elsewhere that he simply answered a newspaper ad seeking a publishing assistant, not knowing it involved comics, let alone his cousin Jean's husband, Martin Goodman:</span>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p><span class="reference-text">I applied for a job in a publishing company ... I didn't even know they published comics. I was fresh out of high school, and I wanted to get into the publishing business, if I could. There was an ad in the paper that said, "Assistant Wanted in a Publishing House." When I found out that they wanted me to assist in comics, I figured, 'Well, I'll stay here for a little while and get some experience, and then I'll get out into the real world.' ... I just wanted to know, 'What do you do in a publishing company?' How do you write? ... How do you publish? I was an assistant. There were two people there named Joe Simon and Jack Kirby – Joe was sort-of the editor/artist/writer, and Jack was the artist/writer. Joe was the senior member. They were turning out most of the artwork. Then there was the publisher, Martin Goodman... And that was about the only staff that I was involved with. After a while, Joe Simon and Jack Kirby left. I was about 17 years old [sic], and Martin Goodman said to me, 'Do you think you can hold down the job of editor until I can find a real person?' When you're 17, what do you know? I said, 'Sure! I can do it!' I think he forgot about me, because I stayed there ever since.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></span></p>
</blockquote>
<p><span class="reference-text">However, in his 2002 autobiography, <i>Excelsior! The Amazing Life of Stan Lee</i> he writes:</span></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p><span class="reference-text">My uncle, Robbie Solomon, told me they might be able to use someone at a publishing company where he worked. The idea of being involved in publishing definitely appealed to me. ... So I contacted the man Robbie said did the hiring, Joe Simon, and applied for a job. He took me on and I began working as a gofer for eight dollars a week....</span></p>
</blockquote>
<p><span class="reference-text">Joe Simon, in his 1990 autobiography <i>The Comic Book Makers</i>, gives the account slightly differently: "One day [Goodman's relative known as] Uncle Robbie came to work with a lanky 17-year-old in tow. 'This is Stanley Lieber, Martin's wife's cousin,' Uncle Robbie said. 'Martin wants you to keep him busy.'"</span></p>
<p><span class="reference-text">In an appendix, however, Simon appears to reconcile the two accounts. He relates a 1989 conversation with Lee:</span></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p><span class="reference-text">Lee: I've been saying this [classified-ad] story for years, but apparently it isn't so. And I can't remember because I['ve] said it so long now that I believe it."<br />
...<br />
Simon: "Your Uncle Robbie brought you into the office one day and he said, 'This is Martin Goodman's wife's nephew.' [sic] ... You were seventeen years old."<br />
<br />
Lee: "Sixteen and a half!"<br />
<br />
Simon: "Well, Stan, you told me seventeen. You were probably trying to be older.... I did hire you."</span></p>
</blockquote>
</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-MCBUR-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-MCBUR_29-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-MCBUR_29-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/Arie_Kaplan" title="Arie Kaplan">Kaplan, Arie</a> (2006). <i>Masters of the Comic Book Universe Revealed!</i>. <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Review_Press" title="Chicago Review Press">Chicago Review Press</a>. p.&#160;50. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-55652-633-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-55652-633-6">978-1-55652-633-6</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AStan+Lee&amp;rft.aufirst=Arie&amp;rft.aulast=Kaplan&amp;rft.btitle=Masters+of+the+Comic+Book+Universe+Revealed%21&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-55652-633-6&amp;rft.pages=50&amp;rft.pub=Chicago+Review+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-SLC-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-SLC_30-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-SLC_30-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">McLaughlin, Jeff; Stan Lee (2007). <i>Stan Lee: Conversations</i>. Jackson, Mississippi: University Press of Mississippi. p.&#160;138. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-57806-985-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-57806-985-9">978-1-57806-985-9</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AStan+Lee&amp;rft.aufirst=Jeff&amp;rft.aulast=McLaughlin&amp;rft.au=Stan+Lee&amp;rft.btitle=Stan+Lee%3A+Conversations&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-57806-985-9&amp;rft.pages=138&amp;rft.place=Jackson%2C+Mississippi&amp;rft.pub=University+Press+of+Mississippi&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Noted comic-book writer <a href="/wiki/Alan_Moore" title="Alan Moore">Alan Moore</a> described the significance of this new approach in a radio interview on the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Four" title="BBC Four">BBC Four</a> program <i>Chain Reaction</i>, transcribed at <cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.comicbookresources.com/?page=article&amp;id=4533">"Alan Moore <i>Chain Reaction</i> Interview Transcript"</a>. <a href="/wiki/Comic_Book_Resources" title="Comic Book Resources">Comic Book Resources</a>. January 27, 2005. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20101108225050/http://www.comicbookresources.com/?page=article&amp;id=4533">Archived</a> from the original on November 8, 2010.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AStan+Lee&amp;rft.btitle=Alan+Moore+Chain+Reaction+Interview+Transcript&amp;rft.date=2005-01-27&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.comicbookresources.com%2F%3Fpage%3Darticle%26id%3D4533&amp;rft.pub=Comic+Book+Resources&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span>:</span>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The DC comics were ... one dimensional characters whose only characteristic was they dressed up in costumes and did good. Whereas Stan Lee had this huge breakthrough of <i>two-</i>dimensional characters. So, they dress up in costumes and do good, but they've got a bad heart. Or a bad leg. I actually did think for a long while that having a bad leg was an actual character trait.</p>
</blockquote>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-wrightp207-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-wrightp207_32-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Wright, Bradford W. (2003). <i>Comic Book Nation: The Transformation of Youth Culture in America</i>. Baltimore, Maryland: The <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins University</a> Press. p.&#160;207. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-8018-7450-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-8018-7450-5">978-0-8018-7450-5</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AStan+Lee&amp;rft.aufirst=Bradford+W.&amp;rft.aulast=Wright&amp;rft.btitle=Comic+Book+Nation%3A+The+Transformation+of+Youth+Culture+in+America&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8018-7450-5&amp;rft.pages=207&amp;rft.place=Baltimore%2C+Maryland&amp;rft.pub=The+Johns+Hopkins+University+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Tom_DeFalco" title="Tom DeFalco">DeFalco, Tom</a> "1960s" in Gilbert (2008), p. 84: "It did not take long for editor Stan Lee to realize that <i>The Fantastic Four</i> was a hit...the flurry of fan letters all pointed to the FF's explosive popularity."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">DeFalco "1960s" in Gilbert (2008), p. 85: "Based on their collaboration on <i>The Fantastic Four</i>, [Stan] Lee worked with Jack Kirby. Instead of a team that fought traditional Marvel monsters however, Lee decided that this time he wanted to feature a monster as the hero."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">DeFalco "1960s" in Gilbert (2008), p. 88: "[Stan Lee] had always been fascinated by the legends of the Norse gods and realized that he could use those tales as the basis for his new series centered on the mighty Thor...The heroic and glamorous style that...Jack Kirby [had] was perfect for Thor."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-36">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">DeFalco "1960s" in Gilbert (2008), p. 91: "Set against the background of the Vietnam War, Iron Man signaled the end of Marvel's monster/suspense line when he debuted in <i>Tales of Suspense</i> #39...[Stan] Lee discussed the general outline for Iron Man with Larry Lieber, who later wrote a full script for the origin story."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-37">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">DeFalco "1960s" in Gilbert (2008), p. 94: "<i>The X-Men</i> #1 introduced the world to Professor Charles Xavier and his teenage students Cyclops, Beast, Angel, Iceman, and Marvel Girl. Magneto, the master of magnetism and future leader of the evil mutants, also appeared."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-38">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">DeFalco "1960s" in Gilbert (2008), p. 100: "Stan Lee chose the name Daredevil because it evoked swashbucklers and circus daredevils, and he assigned Bill Everett, the creator of the Sub-Mariner to design and draw <i>Daredevil</i> #1."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">DeFalco "1960s" in Gilbert (2008), p. 93: [Stan Lee] decided his new superhero feature would star a magician. Since Lee was enjoying his collaborations with Steve Ditko on <i>The Amazing Spider-Man</i>, he decided to assign the new feature to Ditko, who usually handled at least one of the backups in <i>Strange Tales</i>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">DeFalco "1960s" in Gilbert (2008), p. 87: "Deciding that his new character would have spider-like powers, [Stan] Lee commissioned Jack Kirby to work on the first story. Unfortunately, Kirby's version of Spider-Man's alter ego Peter Parker proved too heroic, handsome, and muscular for Lee's everyman hero. Lee turned to Steve Ditko, the regular artist on <i>Amazing Adult Fantasy</i>, who designed a skinny, awkward teenager with glasses."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-wrightp218-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-wrightp218_41-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Wright, p. 218</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-42">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">DeFalco "1960s" in Gilbert (2008), p. 94: "Filled with some wonderful visual action, <i>The Avengers</i> #1 has a very simple story: the Norse god Loki tricked the Hulk into going on a rampage ... The heroes eventually learned about Loki's involvement and united with the Hulk to form the Avengers."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">DeFalco "1960s" in Gilbert (2008), p. 86: "Stan Lee and Jack Kirby reintroduced one of Marvel's most popular Golden Age heroes – Namor, the Sub-Mariner."</span></li>
